commit 860539ec77344fd516943d267d6bc748e1956191
Author: Karsten Sperling <karsten@sperling.co.nz>
Date:   Thu Jun 6 11:08:42 2013 +1200

    Improve handling of popup menus.
    
    * Work around PopupWindow's leaking of listeners into the ViewRoot VTO
      when the anchor view is detached before the popup is dismissed.
    * Apply similar changes to MenuPopupHelper. This also means that support for
      OnAttachStateChangeListener is not required for correct operation of the
      popup window anymore. OnAttachStateChangeListener is still used in case
      the popup anchor view is not attached when the popup is shown, even though
      this seems unlikely to happen in practice as positioning of the popup is
      pretty meaningless in that case. It would be possible to remove the entire
      OnAttachStateChangeListener shim as a second step.
    * Included PopupMenu from AOSP. Technically it's not part of the ActionBar,
      but ABS uses popup menus internally and all the plumbing and resources are
      already in place.

commit c5f968c1a136a940a722f2cfc2a8ef0850de4a69
Author: ChrisSmith <chris.smith324@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Nov 3 03:42:58 2012 -0400

    Fix #652 NPE on sdk < Honeycomb
    
    Calling dispatchRestoreInstanceState from ABS on pre honeycomb causes
    View.java to throw a NPE sometimes becuase ViewGroup.java doesn't do
    this check
    in the older versions. This bug doesn't appear in newer versions of the
    framework.
    
    if ((c.mViewFlags & PARENT_SAVE_DISABLED_MASK) != PARENT_SAVE_DISABLED)
    {
                    c.dispatchRestoreInstanceState(container);
                }
    
    View.java doesn't check for a null container (even on JB) in
    dispatchRestoreInstanceState so it just blows up.

    Check if childIndex is zero being getting previous child

    ViewGroup.getChildAt would catch an exception when a
    invalid index was requested.
    
    Adding a guard at this layer prevents many exceptions
    from being allocated and thrown away at the ViewGroup
    layer.

    Prevent empty overflow popup when there are no overflow items.
    
    On a device with a hardware menu key, an empty overflow window can be displayed
    if there are no items in said overflow menu. This leads to the next user touch
    being swallowed in the action of dismissing the invisible window.
    
    http://b.android.com/27986 & https://android-review.googlesource.com/34700

commit 54fdd6cd21fd7ff715fe24c54e99b302948e5844
Author: Gabriel Ittner <gabriel.ittner@googlemail.com>
Date:   Fri Mar 23 17:42:22 2012 +0100

    added instanceof check

commit e14a1c15caad221770c83b56a6f6d895bc4d91ad
Author: Gabriel Ittner <gabriel.ittner@googlemail.com>
Date:   Fri Mar 23 17:06:38 2012 +0100

    prevent NullPointerException at onTabSelected()
    
    The implementation of onTabSelected() uses the instance variable
    mFragmentTransaction, which is hand over to the listeners
    onTabSelected(). At the start of an Activity, which uses a TabListener
    a NullPointerException is thrown, because the FragmentTransaction is
    null. The only point where a FragmentTransaction is assigned to
    mFragmentTransaction is onTabUnselected().
    
    I guess the intended behavior is that the transaction created in
    onTabUnselected() is used in onTabSelected() afterwards and the
    detaching/attaching is done in the same transaction (because
    onTabUnselected() doesn't call commit on the transaction itself).
    
    However at the start just onTabSelected() is called and not
    onTabUnselected(), because there was nothing selected before. So
    mFragmentTransaction is null and the Exception is thrown. I added an
    if-check to  receive the FragmentTransaction the same way
    onTabUnselected() does, when mFragmentTransaction is null.

commit bd157f8450616546bf74672af477307fd73728f8

    Move support-lib plugin into library.

commit 72b8d9871cab79b512e5c511939a0e54985a480f
Author: Jake Wharton <jakewharton@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 4 21:39:43 2012 -0800

    Handle some interesting cases that occur when using FragmentActivity.
    
     1. When dispatching manually to the superclass onCreatePanelMenu it
        ends up calling onCreateOptionsMenu again. In order to not
        erroneously return true when the application activity returned
        false we use an override Boolean to return the same value as our
        sherlock version.
     2. On pre-Honeycomb the implementation will always return `true`
        since it originally was designed with its own menu support. Since
        we are doing everything ourselves this value can cause incorrect
        results. Instead, use a boolean from the menu which indicates
        whether or not it has any visible menu items. This *should* be
        exactly the same value that would be returned post-Honeycomb.

    Perform relayout on first draw of action menu view.
    
    I am 99% certain this is caused by the ViewRoot (now ViewRootImpl) not receiving a window resized callback when run on the 2.1 platform. This was changed in 2.2 and newer which causes an eager re-measurment of the entire hierarchy.
    
    Closes #272.

commit b8ffe54bf1a49629c2afe79293e6de4ce888430a
Author: Jake Wharton <jakewharton@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Feb 23 02:08:30 2012 -0500

    Action bar sizing fix for Fire, Nook, and original Tab.
    
    Fire and Nook are both large, mdpi, 1024x600 devices. Because of their DPI vs screen size we have plenty of room for a 56dp bar in portrait and 48dp in landscape.
    
    The original Galaxy Tab, however, is a large, hdpi, 1024x600 device. Since the scaling that would occur from the above configuration being picked up creates overly large bars we scale its configuration back down to the normal 48dp/40dp.
    
    Closes #292.

commit e23de78b664be32bcc8888afe338e994bdac6403
Author: Jake Wharton <jakewharton@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Feb 19 23:57:41 2012 -0500

    Change support-lib plugin to allow using binary from Google. Closes #285.
    
    Since its true inception (i.e., version 3), ActionBarSherlock has had one major criticism that created a reluctance for a lot of people to leverage it in their apps: its internalization and modification of the Google support library (compatibility package). This was deemed necessary since there is no reliable external way to dispatch anything to attached and visible fragments.
    
    With this commit we introduce a new set of base classes which exist independent of the support library (and extend from it) in order to progressively add the action bar functionality.
    
     * `SherlockFragmentActivity` replaces `FragmentActivity` and has the job of marshalling our ABS menu classes into native wrappers which can be dispatched along the normal menu callbacks and thus into the appropriate fragments.
     * `SherlockFragment` (and `SherlockListFragment and `SherlockDialogFragment`) replace `Fragment` and unwrap the menu instances dispatched through the fragment manager so that we can use the ABS menu classes in new callbacks. The regular menu callbacks are finalized just like their activity counterparts so that only the correct ones can be overriden.

commit bf43e3ac3ba1c1645e8c45c7692a774b53149367
Author: Jake Wharton <jakewharton@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Feb 17 11:26:05 2012 -0500

    Create a proper plugin system.
    
    Proper plugin-based system for selecting the best implementation of the ActionBarSherlock abstract class. Internally we provide solutions for API 7+ and API 14+ but now we enable future work to be done on providing an API 3+ implementation as well as a TVDPI implementation.
    
    This also comes with the added bonus of being able to expose the implementation of ActionBarSherlock through the `getSherlock()` method (the interface through which static attachment occurs). With this certain window-based properties can be set without requiring explicit methods in the activity base classes. Closes #278.

commit 3d12eaa224f0c7b253b67d80778c3265ce2e302d
Author: Jake Wharton <jakewharton@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Apr 26 12:56:37 2011 -0400

    For the time being, I am including Eclipse .project and .classpath files to ease in using the IDE to develop this library. Until the m2eclipse-android-plugin properly supports
    apklib dependencies as specified by maven, these project files will provide a much easier entry than attempting to set up the projects individually.
    
    Each project should be imported into Eclipse one at a time in the following order:
    
     1. `library/`
     2. `vendor/android_actionbar/actionbar/` and `vendor/greendroid/GreenDroid/`
     3. `handler/android_actionbar/` and `handler/greendroid/`
     4. Sample projects
